<span id="freeTextContainer7763216011157264872">A classical Georgette Heyer's earlier novels have become hugely popular, making THE BLACK MOTH--the fourth of six special Georgette Heyer Collector Editions being offered by Harlequin Books in 2003--an outstanding opportunity for your historical fiction sections. Ms. Heyer wrote THE BLACK MOTH at the young age of 19 and its instant success paved the way for her incredible</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7763216011157264872">A classical Georgette Heyer's earlier novels have become hugely popular, making THE BLACK MOTH--the fourth of six special Georgette Heyer Collector Editions being offered by Harlequin Books in 2003--an outstanding opportunity for your historical fiction sections. Ms. Heyer wrote THE BLACK MOTH at the young age of 19 and its instant success paved the way for her incredible publishing career. Diana Palmer calls Georgette Heyer "a trailblazer" and credits her with shaping her own career. "Heyer's women were spunky, daring and outrageous...her heroes the stuff of dreams."</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_62996617">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62996617" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith" class="left imgcol" title="Sherwood Smith"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1409524068p2/162084.jpg" alt="Sherwood Smith" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62996617?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith" class="user" title="Sherwood Smith">Sherwood Smith</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6602805-the-black-moth" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/162084-sherwood-smith?shelf=siver-fork" class="actionLinkLite">siver-fork</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62996617">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15975480478316235237">This is Georgette Heyer's first pancake. She wrote it as a teen. It's a cliche later silver fork novel with an adventure overlay, showing heavy influence of Orczy and Jeffrey Farnol in particular--but she seems to have discovered that she really liked writing the rakish villain. Because, though this one has the proper ending, the villain is the best character, and she knows it . . . so she rewrote it with the very same sort of villain, but makes him the hero, in <em>These Old Shades</em>. She had also di</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15975480478316235237">This is Georgette Heyer's first pancake. She wrote it as a teen. It's a cliche later silver fork novel with an adventure overlay, showing heavy influence of Orczy and Jeffrey Farnol in particular--but she seems to have discovered that she really liked writing the rakish villain. Because, though this one has the proper ending, the villain is the best character, and she knows it . . . so she rewrote it with the very same sort of villain, but makes him the hero, in <em>These Old Shades</em>. She had also discovered humor and wit by then. This one is really only worth reading as a curiosity, imo.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15975480478316235237">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_78349476">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78349476" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2299418-jenny" class="left imgcol" title="Jenny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1242410017p2/2299418.jpg" alt="Jenny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/78349476?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 19, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2299418-jenny" class="user" title="Jenny">Jenny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth" title="Paperback 9780553132397" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2299418-jenny?shelf=adult-romance" class="actionLinkLite">adult-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer78349476">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10216253971448213775">Oh novel, how do I object to thee? Let me count the ways...<br /><br />1. The title is a phrase that refers to the villian that is mentioned ONLY ONCE over the course of the novel. And it has something to do with the way he dresses. Really, guys? Can't we come up with something more, you know, <em>related</em> to the story?<br />2. The villian is a jerk who tries to kidnap and ravish our poor heroine twice... and receives absolutely no punishment at the end, unless you count the fact that the hero gets the girl and not hi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10216253971448213775">Oh novel, how do I object to thee? Let me count the ways...<br /><br />1. The title is a phrase that refers to the villian that is mentioned ONLY ONCE over the course of the novel. And it has something to do with the way he dresses. Really, guys? Can't we come up with something more, you know, <em>related</em> to the story?<br />2. The villian is a jerk who tries to kidnap and ravish our poor heroine twice... and receives absolutely no punishment at the end, unless you count the fact that the hero gets the girl and not him. Everyone just stands around in his house and shakes their heads at him, but there are no repercussions, legal or social. Seriously?? <br />3. Our hero lets his slimy little weakling of a brother foist the blame of a crooked card game onto his shoulders... and justs accepts it, flees the country for a while, and then becomes a highwayman. *sigh* Protecting your siblings is all well and good, but this is taking nobility to a ridiculous degree. Not impressive. <br />4. The slimy little weakling of a brother is married to perhaps the most annoying woman ever. And he's totally in love with her and makes excuses for her terrible behavior and just <em>lets her get away with it</em>.<br />5. Our heroine is... unmemorable. I'm sure there was some reason that everyone wanted her, but I certainly can't remember what it was. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10216253971448213775">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good" class="left imgcol" title="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389962215p2/16734001.jpg" alt="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/813028851?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good" class="user" title="Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)">Kitty (I solemnly swear that I am up to no good)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth" title="Paperback 9780553132397" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=romance-is-not-dead" class="actionLinkLite">romance-is-not-dead</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=guilty-pleasure" class="actionLinkLite">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/16734001-kitty-i-solemnly-swear-that-i-am-up-to-no-good?shelf=saw-that-one-coming" class="actionLinkLite">saw-that-one-coming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer813028851">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12844646495731754424">This book is hard to review! On one hand, I want to lay into it and point out all the obvious flaws, but on the other hand I am reminded that this was Heyer's first novel at a very young age...so I'm going to argue both points!<br /><br />First hand: <br />This book is rambling and ridiculous, the characters are all lords and ladies...or more like caricatures of lords and ladies, over exaggerated, unconvincing and a little embarrassing.<br />There was no clear cut drive for the novel, it swapped between plots in a way</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12844646495731754424">This book is hard to review! On one hand, I want to lay into it and point out all the obvious flaws, but on the other hand I am reminded that this was Heyer's first novel at a very young age...so I'm going to argue both points!<br /><br />First hand: <br />This book is rambling and ridiculous, the characters are all lords and ladies...or more like caricatures of lords and ladies, over exaggerated, unconvincing and a little embarrassing.<br />There was no clear cut drive for the novel, it swapped between plots in a way that was too complex for Heyer's skills at that time.<br />Our Hero kept on passing out, and our heroine was boring.<br />There was no retribution for the 'Black Moth's' attempted rape...he should have been hanged and scandal be damned. What a bunch of idiots.<br /><br />Second hand:<br />This was her first book and she wrote it to amuse her brother on his sick bed, and this book is with out a doubt amusing! Very swashbuckling, with some fun, trashy romance.<br />She must have gone to great lengths to find research all the regency stuff and it is a massive project to undertake just to cheer your brother up!<br />I read it the whole way through and generally found it quite fun.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12844646495731754424">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/504804360?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 12, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16386700-aslaug-g-rbitz" class="user" title="Aslaug Gørbitz">Aslaug Gørbitz</a>

          <a href="/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth" title="Paperback 9780553132397" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who wishes they could travel back in time.</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/16386700-aslaug-g-rbitz?shelf=favorite" class="actionLinkLite">favorite</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer504804360">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7903596269316923431">My rating system:<br />*Hate it.<br />**Nothing there to like.<br />***Not a favorite, but readable and others might like it and usually do.<br />****I really like it, but it is not to be confused with a true genius.<br />*****True Genius.<br /><br /><br />Unlike other Georgette Heyer fans, this is one of my favorite novels. <br />I first read it many years ago when I was 13 years old. I recently re-read it and found that I liked it just as much now. The first chapter is hard to read as it brandies about so many names, I had to read it twice. I rem</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7903596269316923431">My rating system:<br />*Hate it.<br />**Nothing there to like.<br />***Not a favorite, but readable and others might like it and usually do.<br />****I really like it, but it is not to be confused with a true genius.<br />*****True Genius.<br /><br /><br />Unlike other Georgette Heyer fans, this is one of my favorite novels. <br />I first read it many years ago when I was 13 years old. I recently re-read it and found that I liked it just as much now. The first chapter is hard to read as it brandies about so many names, I had to read it twice. I remember I had to read it twice years ago as well, just to sort out who is who. But after you get the characters straight, this is a wonderful book.<br /><br />I totally fell in love with this hero, and yes he is a genuine hero, not just the main male character. The hero is an honorable man, thief yes, yet honorable nonetheless. His love for his brother, and the sacrifice he makes for him is something I have witnessed firsthand between brothers in my own family, so I could totally relate. Sir Anthony Ferndale is a great name for the hero, even if it is not his real name; personally I prefer it to his own name. He is witty and humorous in his remarks and actions, even if he is a little too free with his kisses for my taste; but that makes sense so it must be forgiven him.<br /><br />The main female character is not a heroine in the strictest sense of the word, but she is true to the time and era of the story, and therefore I like her better than if she was a "heroine" in her own right. The worst that can be said about her is that she is very naïve, but then she is also quite young.<br /><br />I love how Heyer stays true to the era with the language and descriptions. It feels so much more authentic and you truly feel transported to that time and place. I love that it has nothing modern about it. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7503586057820856594">I gather this was the first novel Heyer published, but I only got to it after having read some of her later novels. What was interesting was the way this book seemed to lay out the prototype for <a title="These Old Shades (Alistair, #1) by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades__Alistair___1_">These Old Shades</a> -- the titular "Black Moth" or Tracy "Devil" Belmanoir, is clearly the blueprint for The Duke of Avon, Justin "Satanas" Alistair, including the abduction referred to in Avon's past in These Old Shades, carried out by Belmanoir in The Black Moth. <br /><br />I liked The Black Moth, but it was not as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7503586057820856594">I gather this was the first novel Heyer published, but I only got to it after having read some of her later novels. What was interesting was the way this book seemed to lay out the prototype for <a title="These Old Shades (Alistair, #1) by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades__Alistair___1_">These Old Shades</a> -- the titular "Black Moth" or Tracy "Devil" Belmanoir, is clearly the blueprint for The Duke of Avon, Justin "Satanas" Alistair, including the abduction referred to in Avon's past in These Old Shades, carried out by Belmanoir in The Black Moth. <br /><br />I liked The Black Moth, but it was not as accomplished as her later works -- first, it takes place in the 18th century rather than the 19th, and all of Heyer's books set in the 19th century are generally a little slower and written a little more ploddingly. Second, the characters also feel more unformed than they do in later books like Frederica, The Grand Sophy, Cotillion, etc. and the humor inherent in many of Heyer's books is missing here.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_268155763">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268155763" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim" class="left imgcol" title="Olga Godim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442639299p2/7438487.jpg" alt="Olga Godim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/268155763?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim" class="user" title="Olga Godim">Olga Godim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7438487-olga-godim?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer268155763">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3417935538983611240">This was the first novel by Heyer, and also it had its share of problems, it read very well, showing the hand of the future master of the romance genre.<br />The novel is set not during Regency – that period will be introduced into Heyer’s fiction later – but vaguely in the middle of the 18th century. Traveling to the continent is still sort-of a fashion for British aristocracy, and no one heard of Napoleon yet. Life is peaceful, except for our hero, Jack.<br />Seven years ago, Jack and his younger brother</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3417935538983611240">This was the first novel by Heyer, and also it had its share of problems, it read very well, showing the hand of the future master of the romance genre.<br />The novel is set not during Regency – that period will be introduced into Heyer’s fiction later – but vaguely in the middle of the 18th century. Traveling to the continent is still sort-of a fashion for British aristocracy, and no one heard of Napoleon yet. Life is peaceful, except for our hero, Jack.<br />Seven years ago, Jack and his younger brother Richard participated in a card game. Richard cheated. When the cheating was discovered, Jack, who loved his baby brother dearly, took the blame and became social pariah. Now he roams the English countryside, occasionally posing as a highwayman and robing fat merchants. He misses the society and his ancestral home but bravely refrains from fixing his situation, ready to sacrifice everything for his brother’s happiness... until he meets Diana, the heroine, and falls in love. Then his sacrifice becomes an unbearable burden, but what can a noble hero do? <br />Sadly, neither Jack nor Diana are really the protagonists of this tale. The book’s title actually refers to the bad guy, a cynical and slightly sinister Duke of Andover. With his nickname Black Moth, he is the antagonist of the story. That’s in a nutshell the problem of this book. It lacks focus and the clearly defined lead characters. <br />More often than not, the author concentrates not on Jack or Diana but either on the sardonic black-clad Duke or on Jack’s brother, weak but squirming from the pangs of conscience Richard. Or even on Richard’s wife, capricious and empty headed creature Lavinia. Hardly any time or page space is given to our sympathetic but or-so-honorable hero and heroine. <br />Eventually, good guys prevailed, of course, and love triumphed, but the entire book has a feel of Victorian fiction much more than the 20th century literature, which is understandable. It was published in the transitional period, in 1921, and Heyer herself still needed some experience to rise to the heights of her talent and become the founder of modern romance genre. She was still learning the craft.<br />What struck me in this book was the double standards exercised by British aristocrats. I don’t remember reading about it in any other Heyer’s novel, but here it’s naked and repulsive. <br />After the card cheating incident, Jack spent some time in Europe, making his living as a fencing teacher. That time is behind him now, but he still bemoans it bitterly: that he, a British earl, had to teach fencing. It was a horrible time for him. I read about it and thought: why? It was an honest occupation. But obviously not for a nobleman, right? <br />The Duke of Andover (the villain, remember) once fought a sword duel with a commoner, or at least a man he thought a commoner. After the faux commoner won, the duke accepted his defeat, gave up his sword, and then, after his adversary turned away, he shot him.<br />Afterwards, the characters discuss this episode and come to the conclusion that the duke definitely didn’t know that his opponent belonged to the aristocracy too. He would never have shot him otherwise. Not even Black Moth would stoop to such dishonor. <br />And again, I wonder. It’s dishonorable to break your word to another aristocrat but it’s okay to betray your word to a commoner? Some honor! <br />Still, I enjoyed this book. For all its flaws, it was an entertaining tale and definitely a must-read for all Heyer’s and historical romance fans. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3417935538983611240">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_852772145">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/852772145" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4368838-caz" class="left imgcol" title="Caz"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1332962126p2/4368838.jpg" alt="Caz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/852772145?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4368838-caz" class="user" title="Caz">Caz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17690232-the-black-moth" title="Audio CD 9781843797593" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=romance-other" class="actionLinkLite">romance-other</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=4-5-stars" class="actionLinkLite">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=oldies-but-goodies" class="actionLinkLite">oldies-but-goodies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=audiogals" class="actionLinkLite">audiogals</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4368838-caz?shelf=romance-pre-1800s" class="actionLinkLite">romance-pre-1800s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer852772145">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer985393088745716810"><strong>I've given this a B for content, and an A- for narration at AudioGals, so I'm calling it 4.5 stars all together.</strong><br /><br />Although I’m a long-term reader and fan of Georgette Heyer’s romances, there are a couple that, for reasons I can’t fathom, passed me by, and <strong>The Black Moth</strong> is one of them. So I’ve come to the audio completely fresh, as it were, not having read the book previously. I don’t know if that’s made a difference to my perception of it: looking at the number of poor-to-middling reviews on Good</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText985393088745716810"><strong>I've given this a B for content, and an A- for narration at AudioGals, so I'm calling it 4.5 stars all together.</strong><br /><br />Although I’m a long-term reader and fan of Georgette Heyer’s romances, there are a couple that, for reasons I can’t fathom, passed me by, and <strong>The Black Moth</strong> is one of them. So I’ve come to the audio completely fresh, as it were, not having read the book previously. I don’t know if that’s made a difference to my perception of it: looking at the number of poor-to-middling reviews on Goodreads makes me wonder if it has, because I thought this audiobook was a delight from start to finish.<br /><br />The storytelling itself isn’t perfect and the action does jump around a bit. That said however, I was so quickly wrapped up in the story of the honourable Earl who lies to protect his brother and do right by the woman they both want to marry, that I was more or less unaware of any abrupt cuts or shifts of POV.<br /><br />The Black Moth is Heyer’s first published novel, and on the whole, is an incredibly assured piece of work for a nineteen-year-old. Yes, there are things that speak of her youth. For example, some of the characterisation is weak, there are some parts of the book in which there is far more telling than showing, and there is the aforementioned jumping around but overall, I found this to be an enjoyable and rewarding listen.<br /><br />One of the things I particularly enjoy about reading and listening to books that were written decades ago is the way in which the authors seemed more able to take their time to set up their stories and to build their characters. I remember saying something similar in my review of <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.audiogals.net/2013/09/the-devil-on-horseback-by-victoria-holt/#.UwNi2k3ivIU">The Devil on Horseback</a> by Victoria Holt; perhaps to a younger reader or listener, this is “slow”, but for me, it’s a luxurious experience, and something to be savoured.<br /><br />The story itself is fairly simple. Six years previously the hero, Jack Carstares, Earl of Wyncham, was accused of cheating at cards and, having admitted his guilt to such a terrible breach of the code of honour, fled the country. I suppose such a thing is inconceivable today, but it seems such things were taken very seriously back in the 18th century! Jack has spent the intervening years roaming Europe living on his wits and from his ill-gotten gains as a Gentleman of the Road – or highwayman. The thing is – Jack wasn’t guilty. He was covering up for his younger brother who, in a fit of panic, had been desperate enough to cheat and who, when Jack was accused, said nothing.<br /><br />Jack’s brother, Richard, married the lovely Lavinia, who leads him a merry dance, being petulant and demanding, and as the years have progressed, he has become more and more weighed down by his guilt. And then, one year ago, the brothers met again when Jack unknowingly held up Richard’s coach, and since then, Richard has been struggling with his conscience even more.<br /><br />For his part, Jack has not been too sorry with the way his life has panned out until he rescues a damsel in distress from the evil clutches of the villain, falls in love, and realises he has nothing to offer her.<br /><br />You can read the rest of this review at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.audiogals.net/2014/02/the-black-moth-by-georgette-heyer/#.UwdDcE3ivIU">AudioGals</a><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="985393088745716810">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_292789480">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292789480" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5812187-jewels-my-devastating-reads" class="left imgcol" title="Jewels ? My Devastating Reads"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446383281p2/5812187.jpg" alt="Jewels ? My Devastating Reads" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/292789480?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5812187-jewels-my-devastating-reads" class="user" title="Jewels ? My Devastating Reads">Jewels ? My Devastating Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth" title="Paperback 9780553132397" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer292789480">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8803839795963292137">I had a hard time making sense of this book. It's the first book I've read by this author, and I understand it was the first novel she wrote, at a rather young age. I couldn't even really decide what sort of a rating to give this read. I think it's more of a two and half star read. <br /><br />Heyer spins an entertaining tale, I'll say that much for this novel. But at times the entertainment value wans as you have to wonder what the hell this is about. Is it a love story? Yes and no. It's not really about D</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8803839795963292137">I had a hard time making sense of this book. It's the first book I've read by this author, and I understand it was the first novel she wrote, at a rather young age. I couldn't even really decide what sort of a rating to give this read. I think it's more of a two and half star read. <br /><br />Heyer spins an entertaining tale, I'll say that much for this novel. But at times the entertainment value wans as you have to wonder what the hell this is about. Is it a love story? Yes and no. It's not really about Diana and Jack however. Nor is it really about Jack and his brother and their huge "scandal". It's also not really about the amoral villain, the black moth, Devil the Duke of Andover. These characters are all ridiculous in their way, but compelling as well. Overall the book seemed to lack substance but like a soap opera, you can't seem to give up on it. And like a soap opera, the villain gets away with his crime, foiled though it might have been. Luckily, unlike a soap opera, it ends eventually and rather happily for all the characters you want it to. <br /><br />Note: this novel can easily be placed into the genre if Gothic lit, not romance as we understand it today. From the prologue and epilogue I got the feeling that this story was supposed to cure Devil of his evil ways but the rest of the novel didn't do a good job in portraying characters and circumstances to lead me to believe that he actually has learned some great lesson. But, the writing was sharp and witty and I'll read more of Heyer as I'm sure her later novels are better. <br /><br />More reviews at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.devastatingreads.blogspoot.com" target="_blank">www.devastatingreads.blogspoot.com</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8803839795963292137">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_118560548">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118560548" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" title="Wealhtheow"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" alt="Wealhtheow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/118560548?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="user" title="Wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2899966-the-black-moth" title="Paperback 9780373773398" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer118560548">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17388190443115189370">When he was young, Jack Carstares took the blame when his younger brother was caught cheating at cards. He was ostracized from society and fled to the Continent, where he eventually made his fortune gambling and teaching fencing. Now he has returned to England, where he plays at being a highwayman (but in fact, gives all his ill-gotten gains to the poor). When his younger brother realizes that Jack is back, he is wracked with guilt, but as before his love for the spoiled Lavinia keeps him from r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17388190443115189370">When he was young, Jack Carstares took the blame when his younger brother was caught cheating at cards. He was ostracized from society and fled to the Continent, where he eventually made his fortune gambling and teaching fencing. Now he has returned to England, where he plays at being a highwayman (but in fact, gives all his ill-gotten gains to the poor). When his younger brother realizes that Jack is back, he is wracked with guilt, but as before his love for the spoiled Lavinia keeps him from revealing the truth.<br /><br />Meanwhile, the Duke of Andover (called Devil by friends and foes alike) has fallen for young Diana. He woos her under a false name, then tries to abduct her--but Jack, in his guise as a highwayman, fights him back. The Duke returns to London to come up with another plan to get Diana into his clutches, and Jack and Diana fall in love while she nurses him from his wounds. But Jack is still unwilling to cast aside his bad reputation, and so he and Diana cannot get married. Alack! It all ends happily, of course.<br /><br />This is a very odd book. First off, the morality system is quite strange: when Jack is accused of cheating at cards his friends and family cast him out entirely. But the Duke can try to seduce, abduct, and full on rape a lady *repeatedly*, and no one considers so much as disinviting him from a party. Nor, in fact, will Jack even reveal the Duke's real name to the woman he tried to ruin--he puts actual effort into keeping the Duke's true identity a secret. Madness!<br /><br />The other oddity is that the male friendships are given so much more intensity and page time than the romance between Jack and Diana. Jack and his valet Jim have an adorably/uncomfortably (depending on your feelings about class differences) feudal relationship. A great deal of the book is made up of conversations between Jack and O'Hara, who adore each other, banter constantly, and defend each other viciously. And, of course, there is the Duke and his bff Fortescue. The book opens with a letter from the Duke to Fortescue, and finishes with the Duke and Fortescue talking in their shared lodging in Venice. The Duke says Fortescue is literally the only person he likes in the whole world, and Fortescue spends all his time hanging out with the Duke, trying to get him to talk about his feelings. <br /><br />Although Diana does not get nearly the amount of page time the menfolk do (and in fact, Lavinia and O'Hara's wife get about as much page time as she does), she's a good character. She particularly shines in her final showdown with the Duke. But as for the Duke himself--I don't get why Heyer would want to write this character again, nor why anyone finds him fascinating. He's just another drawling menacing asshole, another Marquis St. Evrémonde or Lucius Malfoy. Maybe I'm just tired of the type, which seems to be everywhere in Regency romances.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17388190443115189370">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_452634567">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/452634567" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5134198-jenna" class="left imgcol" title="Jenna"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389772832p2/5134198.jpg" alt="Jenna" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/452634567?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5134198-jenna" class="user" title="Jenna">Jenna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth" title="Paperback 9780553132397" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5134198-jenna?shelf=meet-cute" class="actionLinkLite">meet-cute</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5134198-jenna?shelf=its-history" class="actionLinkLite">its-history</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5134198-jenna?shelf=listen-to-this" class="actionLinkLite">listen-to-this</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5134198-jenna?shelf=swashes-and-buckles" class="actionLinkLite">swashes-and-buckles</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5134198-jenna?shelf=hey-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">hey-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer452634567">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4016903200559483434">3.5 stars.<br /><br />The fact that Georgette Heyer wrote this at 17 is pretty astonishing. It's such a delightful book which, while perhaps not as polished as her later works, firmly establishes the charm and humour she would display throughout her career.<br /><br />Heyer apparently first invented the story to tell to her sick younger brother, and it contains all the classic elements you'd expect from such an origin - an engaging hero who flirts with danger but actually has a heart of gold, a beautiful heroine who ca</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4016903200559483434">3.5 stars.<br /><br />The fact that Georgette Heyer wrote this at 17 is pretty astonishing. It's such a delightful book which, while perhaps not as polished as her later works, firmly establishes the charm and humour she would display throughout her career.<br /><br />Heyer apparently first invented the story to tell to her sick younger brother, and it contains all the classic elements you'd expect from such an origin - an engaging hero who flirts with danger but actually has a heart of gold, a beautiful heroine who captures said heart, a ~dastardly~ villain you love to hate, lots of action, scandal and intrigue, plus a bit of bromance on top of all that.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the characters, especially Jack and his best friend Miles, and I even empathised with the tiresome Lady Lavinia. One of my favourite things about Heyer's writing is not the lavish period descriptions or even the melodrama (though they're great too), but the connections between the characters. Whether it's sibling bonds (or lack thereof), enemies, friends, married couples or people just falling in love, the relationships always feel so very real and universal, enhanced by the witty and engaging dialogue.<br /><br />I listened to the audiobook narrated by Julian Rhind-Tutt and he does an excellent job. The voices he gives to each character are strong - the male characters in particular - and his pacing and delivery are good.<br /><br />The story was a little uneven and frankly quite baffling in places (the reason Jack had to leave the country seemed weak, for instance, though maybe I'm imposing too modern a judgement), but overall <em>The Black Moth</em> was a fun read and a great way to start my quest to consume all of Heyer's romances.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4016903200559483434">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/96192502?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 06, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/912349-aphie" class="user" title="Aphie">Aphie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2626949-the-black-moth" title="Paperback 9780330200929" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/912349-aphie?shelf=period-novel" class="actionLinkLite">period-novel</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer96192502">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10236935525725260497">As all the other reviews on this site can't wait to tell you, <em>The Black Moth</em> was Georgette Heyer's first novel, and it really does show. The character descriptions read like a gifted teenager wrote them (oddly enough) with an emphasis on how beautful the hero, heroine and villain all are, and the !drama! and !action! is fairly heavy-handed.<br /><br />That said, it's not a <strong>bad</strong> novle. It reminds me most strongly of of the style in <em>The Reluctant Widow</em>, only instead of light-hearted banter and scrapes courtesy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10236935525725260497">As all the other reviews on this site can't wait to tell you, <em>The Black Moth</em> was Georgette Heyer's first novel, and it really does show. The character descriptions read like a gifted teenager wrote them (oddly enough) with an emphasis on how beautful the hero, heroine and villain all are, and the !drama! and !action! is fairly heavy-handed.<br /><br />That said, it's not a <strong>bad</strong> novle. It reminds me most strongly of of the style in <em>The Reluctant Widow</em>, only instead of light-hearted banter and scrapes courtesy of a younger brother in law there's hysteria and irritation from the sister in law that the hero was supposed to have previously been in love with.<br /><br />I found myself asking "Why?" over the text more often than not. WHY was the sister in law so sought after by the two brothers when she was so obviously a vapid ninny? WHY did the hero decide to become a highwayman, exactly? WHY did everyone want the bland heroine who didn't seem to do or say a single remarkable thing? WHY was The Black Moth of the title so evil and callous? And WHY was I asking, since he read like a melodrama villain - just missing the moustachios to twirl.<br /><br /><br />My favourite charcter was the hero's valet.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_410043905">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410043905" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7632663-alice" class="left imgcol" title="Alice"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1328556026p2/7632663.jpg" alt="Alice" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/410043905?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7632663-alice" class="user" title="Alice">Alice</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6963840-the-black-moth" title="Paperback 9781402219528" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7632663-alice?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer410043905">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11562329461284813138">I have been putting off getting back to my reviews for so long, that this one may be a bit choppy, as the story is not as clear in my brain anymore. :P Please forgive. ;) But I did write down some points to hit so I'll follow those! :D<br /><br />One thing I loved about The Black Moth was the theme of loyalty in the family. Our family is the best and closest earthly thing we have, and they deserve our utmost loyalty! Especially the two brothers in this story, really got this point across. Both of them staye</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11562329461284813138">I have been putting off getting back to my reviews for so long, that this one may be a bit choppy, as the story is not as clear in my brain anymore. :P Please forgive. ;) But I did write down some points to hit so I'll follow those! :D<br /><br />One thing I loved about The Black Moth was the theme of loyalty in the family. Our family is the best and closest earthly thing we have, and they deserve our utmost loyalty! Especially the two brothers in this story, really got this point across. Both of them stayed loyal to the other by keeping things quiet that could cause ruin for their sibling but gain for themselves, to keep each other safe- and in the end everything worked out. :)<br />Dicks wife Lavinia REALLY got on my nerves for the better part of this book! She was so annoying and demanding- she kept bringing to mind that verse in the Bible that says "A continual dropping in a very rainy day and a contentious woman are alike." ;P But she was another aspect of the book that I ended up really liking, and it played along with the loyalty theme. Her transformation was really sweet to watch, and I felt so happy for Dick in the end- knowing he had truly loved her from the very start, and never let her down, even when she was horrid and selfish. <br />The hero of our story- Lord John Carstares- reminded me a lot of Wesley, from The Princess Bride. Calm, daring, servant-hearted, great sense of humor, disguises! :D I really enjoyed his character.<br />Diana, seemed to me to be put out more as a secondary character than as the heroine- like she was there merely as a love interest for the hero. Being a love interest and being a heroine are two completely different things- so I would have to say the title would go to Lavinia, who got most of the limelight. However I did really enjoy Diana's character! I liked that she was bold and confidant, but also sweet tempered and positive. :)<br />There was definitely no mistaking our villain! Tracy was so conniving and mean in that smooth-and-creepy way. I was glad Diana could tell from the start that he was bad news- I can't stand a 'heroine' who is completely oblivious to what everyone else around her can see clear as day (when it comes to spotting the villain). I was glad that he lived in the end- another score for the hero- because he was able to make up with his siblings and carry on the family theme, and actually apologize to the heroine for being so nasty, but still got his punishment, as he deserved (another thing I can't stand is a villain who gets off completely without even being reprimanded). <br />My favorite couple from this story was Miles and Molly. They were so sweeeet!!! :D<br />The ending to this story was hilarious! Most comedic way to make everything lighthearted and involve all the characters at once that I've ever read. Well done. :)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11562329461284813138">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_581426459">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581426459" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18780551-anne" class="left imgcol" title="Anne"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1437261844p2/18780551.jpg" alt="Anne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/581426459?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18780551-anne" class="user" title="Anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6963840-the-black-moth" title="Paperback 9781402219528" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=georgian" class="actionLinkLite">georgian</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=young-heroines" class="actionLinkLite">young-heroines</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=gentleman-like-heroes" class="actionLinkLite">gentleman-like-heroes</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=role-model-heroines" class="actionLinkLite">role-model-heroines</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=swashbucklers" class="actionLinkLite">swashbucklers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer581426459">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13075862415140933036">This was my very first Heyer novel and I must admit that I was immensely impressed. I totally loved this book, even though I agree with some of the reviewers who have said that it is not her best effort. Having read a few other of her novels, I can see that now, but I still had to give this one 5 stars, because I enjoyed it so much when I read it! I thought the ending was ridiculous though; the way she wrapped up the whole affair with Jack, Diana and the villain...really it was poorly done. The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13075862415140933036">This was my very first Heyer novel and I must admit that I was immensely impressed. I totally loved this book, even though I agree with some of the reviewers who have said that it is not her best effort. Having read a few other of her novels, I can see that now, but I still had to give this one 5 stars, because I enjoyed it so much when I read it! I thought the ending was ridiculous though; the way she wrapped up the whole affair with Jack, Diana and the villain...really it was poorly done. The whole book was good, very much dramatic and over-the-top and then the ending comes and she concludes it by kinda just making everybody stop whatever they're doing, and making them all go to dinner...It was like huh and the villain?? When does he learn his lesson??<br /><br />I also agree that the females were pretty poorly represented...She did not honour her own sex in this one! Lavinia is a spoiled, ridiculous, melodramatic wife, who makes both herself and her husband unhappy. Diana is too perfect; she doesn't really do anything, she's just there, yet everyone loves her and every ones wants her. I thought Lady O'Hara to be pretty decent and she could be quite funny at times.<br /><br />The main hero wasn't much developed either, or should I say, not like her other heroes, but I had the impression that he was agreeable enough; handsome, noble, generous. His younger brother made a good character, he was extremely weak and had not a strong will of his own. I personally really liked the villain, he was definitely one of my favourite characters.<br /><br />So if overall the characters were OK, how come I loved this novel so much? Georgette Heyer is a master of writing, and not knowing what to expect, I found the period details (clothes, places, etc...) simply irresistible! Add in her humour and her signature witty style and it makes this book well worth the read even if she has done much better since. A must-read for Heyer fans.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13075862415140933036">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer121403623">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17073811740501192654">I have a lot of complaints about this book, but there's still something to love in the idea of a society where being a highwayman for years is more forgivable than cheating at cards.<br /><br />John Carstares is an Earl, a highwayman, and a social outcast, thanks to his decision to take the blame for his brother's attempt to cheat at cards. Richard, the guilty brother, wants to set the record straight, but that could put his marriage at risk. Their story also includes a villainous Duke, a fiery young beauty</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17073811740501192654">I have a lot of complaints about this book, but there's still something to love in the idea of a society where being a highwayman for years is more forgivable than cheating at cards.<br /><br />John Carstares is an Earl, a highwayman, and a social outcast, thanks to his decision to take the blame for his brother's attempt to cheat at cards. Richard, the guilty brother, wants to set the record straight, but that could put his marriage at risk. Their story also includes a villainous Duke, a fiery young beauty, a flighty wife, a devoted servant, assorted in-laws, and a friendly but interfering couple.<br /><br />I'm very glad that this wasn't the first Heyer book I read, because I know that she's better than this. Things were too drawn out, and some of the subplots and characters seemed completely unnecessary.<br /><br />I expected forgiveness, but it would have been nice if there had been any real sense of tension between the brothers. The bad guy basically admits to being a serial rapist, so his ending was extremely unsatisfying - especially because all the men in the book seemed to think things were handled so well. I guess that since the others he'd abducted weren't gentlewomen with expert duelists on hand, we aren't supposed to mind what must have happened to them.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17073811740501192654">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_667067706">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/667067706" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear" class="left imgcol" title="QNPoohBear"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1394921233p2/22177907.jpg" alt="QNPoohBear" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/667067706?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 20, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22177907-qnpoohbear" class="user" title="QNPoohBear">QNPoohBear</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2657385-the-black-moth" title="Hardcover 9780434328192" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=clean-romance" class="actionLinkLite">clean-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=georgian-romance" class="actionLinkLite">georgian-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22177907-qnpoohbear?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer667067706">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6598892643537677763"><br />This book reads very much like a first novel and one that would appeal to teens with lots of melodrama, dashing heroes, swordfights and a beautiful heroine. There are many spots were the writing doesn't flow very well and the characters are all pretty much cardboard. There's noble Jack, wicked Tracy, spoiled and selfish Lavinia, intelligent and kind Diana, etc. These character archetypes would be developed into flesh and blood people in later novels but in this first work, Miss Heyer had not yet</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6598892643537677763"><br />This book reads very much like a first novel and one that would appeal to teens with lots of melodrama, dashing heroes, swordfights and a beautiful heroine. There are many spots were the writing doesn't flow very well and the characters are all pretty much cardboard. There's noble Jack, wicked Tracy, spoiled and selfish Lavinia, intelligent and kind Diana, etc. These character archetypes would be developed into flesh and blood people in later novels but in this first work, Miss Heyer had not yet developed her ability to create real people the reader can care about. My favorite characters are Sir and Lady Miles. They're the most well-drawn characters in the novel and seem like people I would actually like to know. The plot is a bit ridiculous and unbelievable and a bit complicated. There are many characters to keep track of and I had to keep turning the page back to find out who was speaking or what was happening. There's lots of sweeping melodrama and adventure but not much romance. We're told that Jack and Diana fall in love but the actual falling in love is glossed over, perhaps because Miss Heyer had not yet been in love or perhaps because she was writing for her kid brother. The historical details are incredibly impressive and fans of historic costuming will die at the descriptions of powder, patch, hoops, wigs and other styles of the mid-18th century. I would recommend this book to those who love an old-fashioned high drama adventure story or to those fans of Miss Heyer who wish to see how her style evolved. It's not a bad effort for a seventeen year old's first novel.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6598892643537677763">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_6904800">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6904800" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days" class="left imgcol" title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/6904800?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 29, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days" class="user" title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6602805-the-black-moth" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=re-read" class="actionLinkLite">re-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=cover-love" class="actionLinkLite">cover-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6904800">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6793458983222480170">At the beginning of the year, I set myself the goal of re-reading all my Heyer books. I have all her books except for her eight detective novels, and I've read all but, I think, two - two of the more serious historical ones: <em>My Lord John</em> and, ah, forget the other. Oh maybe it was just the one then? Well, it's nearly May and so far my progress has been pathetic, to say the least. I read Heyer's books so many times during uni but it's been eight or nine years and I found I couldn't remember the st</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6793458983222480170">At the beginning of the year, I set myself the goal of re-reading all my Heyer books. I have all her books except for her eight detective novels, and I've read all but, I think, two - two of the more serious historical ones: <em>My Lord John</em> and, ah, forget the other. Oh maybe it was just the one then? Well, it's nearly May and so far my progress has been pathetic, to say the least. I read Heyer's books so many times during uni but it's been eight or nine years and I found I couldn't remember the stories anymore - a good time to re-read them! Worked, too.<br /><br />I re-read <em>
  <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.giraffedays.com/?p=231">Beauvallet</a>
</em>, the first Heyer book I ever read, a year or so ago - it's a good one to start with if you've never read any. Most of her books are set in Regency London (during the time of the Prince Regent, George, whose father was mad), but some are set in an earlier period - like <em>The Black Moth</em>. Set sometime mid-1700s, this is also an unusual Heyer novel for the broad cast of characters and lack of a central pair.<br /><br />The "Black Moth", as described by the heroine, Helen, is the Duke of Andover, Tracy Belmanoir - commonly called the Devil. A pale man always dressed in black, he's unashamedly selfish, sneers at others and has only one real friend. He is a central character, an unlikeable one, who connects everyone else.<br /><br />Helen is the only child of a country gentleman who, while in Bath with her aunt, meets the Devil in one of his other guises, as Mr Everard. He repulses her, but he doesn't care about that: if he wants her, he'll have her. Kidnapping seems the way to go.<br /><br />Enter Jack, Lord John Carstares, newly made Earl of Wyncham now that his father is dead - and social outcast, ever since taking the blame when his younger brother Richard cheats at cards. Now back in England, he keeps himself in funds and entertainment by being a highwayman. Masked, he holds up coaches - though, being a man of honour, he doesn't steal from women or old people and gives much of it away to the poor. Encountering a carriage stopped on the road, with three men trying to wrestle a girl from its interior, he doesn't waste time engaging the orchestrator in a duel. He recognises Tracy, a skilled swordsman, but keeps his own incognito and defeats him to boot, suffering an injury in exchange. Helen and her aunt are only too happy for him to recover at their home, and it is during his convalescence that he and Helen fall in love.<br /><br />Meanwhile, his poor brother Richard is reaping the punishments of letting his brother take the rap for his bad choice six years ago. The lovely Lady Lavinia, the Devil's only sister, is almost as selfish, just as extravagant, and prone to fits of temper and moodiness. Richard still loves her, and it's for her sake that he has kept quiet all these years about who really cheated at cards: he can't bring her down with him. But his guilty conscience is ageing him, and it's only a matter of time before he can't tolerate it at all. His marriage is going downhill just as badly, and it seems like everything's coming to an end.<br /><br />Ironically, it is the Black Moth that brings these characters together, pulls them apart, then brings them together again - all without intending it, for the most part. It's a much different structure from her usual Regency Romances, and its originality makes it stand out. The characters are still fairly stock - Heyer only has a few character versions that she recycles, as do most genre authors, and it's never really bothered me. Lord John - Jack - is the delightful, amused, finnicky dresser, the real hero of the story - but flawed all the same. Richard suffers, yes he pays for letting his brother be repudiated and scorned by society, and he's sympathetic for not taking advantage of it (except to marry Lavinia, and he pays for that too - literally and figuratively). There's Jack's best friend Sir Miles and his wife, Lady O'Hara, who are adorable, and Helen of course, who's quick tongue and strong spirit make her a strong heroine even though they attract the Devil's attentions. He, in his own way, is a sympathetic figure. He's despicable, and not at all appealing, but you can't help feeling sorry for him. Still wouldn't want to try to befriend him though. It's a nice change, actually, to encounter an anti-hero as distinctive as Tracy in Heyer's work.<br /><br /><strong>A Note on this Edition:</strong> There were contemporary editions of Heyer's books available when I started collecting them, but they were hard to find and online ordering was not common "in those days" (yes I know, we're talking 1996-2002, the period in which I collected them all, but it's amazing how recent our dependence on the internet really is). Very few were available in bookshops, and I was a poor student anyway. I found most of them at op-shops, secondhand bookshops, and at Salamanca Market. I don't mind having old, yellowed copies with, often, very ugly covers. Amongst them are gems like this one - an Australian second edition with the original dust jacket (some of my Heyer books don't have dust jackets, which is a shame). So, this is a scan of my cover, tattered corners and all. And just look at it! Isn't it beautiful? It's falling apart, sadly, so I have to remove it when reading the book - ironic, since a dust jacket's purpose is to protect the book! <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6793458983222480170">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12591369757271189108">I love the way Georgette Heyer writes. That being said this is not the best of her books. Villain is too villainous. Hero is to willing to let things lie. the writing style may not be for everyone as there are a lot of descriptions of people, places, outfits, and food. As always I laughed a lot while reading. This is one of the few authors whose books I buy because I reread her books.<br /><br />1/2013 Just reread as I needed a change of pace. I'd forgotten how much I loved this book. It made me laugh as al</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12591369757271189108">I love the way Georgette Heyer writes. That being said this is not the best of her books. Villain is too villainous. Hero is to willing to let things lie. the writing style may not be for everyone as there are a lot of descriptions of people, places, outfits, and food. As always I laughed a lot while reading. This is one of the few authors whose books I buy because I reread her books.<br /><br />1/2013 Just reread as I needed a change of pace. I'd forgotten how much I loved this book. It made me laugh as always. Clean romance and well written romance that focuses on love rather than sex/lust was just what I needed to help clear my mind. Reading another Heyer book before I get back to all the library books I have that are due back in the next couple of weeks. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1198410017">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198410017" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat" class="left imgcol" title="Damaskcat"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395844674p2/6945307.jpg" alt="Damaskcat" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1198410017?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6945307-damaskcat" class="user" title="Damaskcat">Damaskcat</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/9515440-the-black-moth" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1198410017">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13668822476252148715">I first read 'The Black Moth' more than forty years ago and decided then that it wasn't one of my favourite Heyer novels. I have just re-read it and still class it as one of my least favourite. It is set in the eighteenth century and not the period she made quintessentially her own, the Regency, so I suppose it starts off with a disadvantage from my point of view.<br /><br />The book lacks, in the main, the author's famous lightness of touch and her humour, though towards the end there are flashes of it as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13668822476252148715">I first read 'The Black Moth' more than forty years ago and decided then that it wasn't one of my favourite Heyer novels. I have just re-read it and still class it as one of my least favourite. It is set in the eighteenth century and not the period she made quintessentially her own, the Regency, so I suppose it starts off with a disadvantage from my point of view.<br /><br />The book lacks, in the main, the author's famous lightness of touch and her humour, though towards the end there are flashes of it as the tragedy descends almost into farce as the various relationships are resolved. <br /><br />The Duke of Andover falls in love with the beautiful Diana and instead of courting her in the normal fashion he decides to kidnap her. Unfortunately for him Diana finds him sinister and unsettling and anyway she has fallen in love with someone else - the pleasant and likeable 'Mr Carr' with his secret past and disreputable present.<br /><br />The book owes at least some of its inspiration I think to the tales of Gothic horror fashionable later in the eighteenth century with the sinister looking Duke dressed all in black and known as The Black Moth. The kidnap is straight out of Mrs Edgeworth or 'Monk' Lewis as is the Duke's sinister appearance.<br /><br />This is an enjoyable read though and puts many authors of historical novels in the shade but it isn't a good introduction to Georgette Heyer. If you want to start reading her novels then 'Arabella' or 'Friday's Child' are good books to start with.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13668822476252148715">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
